the San Francisco-based utility group, is planning to file for bankruptcy as it struggles to cope with the costs of the devastating wildfires that swept through northern California in 2017 and 2018.

Shares in PG&E almost halved on Monday after the company said that it would enter Chapter 11 bankruptcy protection on or about January 29, raising the pressure on California‚Äôs state government to come up with a restructuring plan to support its operations.

PG&E has looked increasingly likely to file for bankruptcy as evidence has emerged of its role in the Camp fire in northern California last year, which killed at least 86 people. The California Department of Forestry and Fire Protection identified the first signs of the Camp fire near a tower on one of PG&E‚Äôs transmission lines, and the company said it had seen damage and a ‚Äúflash mark‚Äù on that tower.

PG&E said bankruptcy protection would enable it to maintain gas and electricity supplies for customers and work out its liabilities from the wildfires, which it has estimated at more than $30bn.

But lawmakers in California are concerned that in bankruptcy PG&E might not be able to invest to meet the state‚Äôs energy policy goals, including a shift to 100 per cent renewable power and infrastructure for electric vehicles.
